Overview\n\nThe Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:\n\n- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag\n- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow\n- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode\n- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout\n\nThis migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior\n\n**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required\n\nIn v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:\n```protobuf\n// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:\n```protobuf\n// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache\n  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache\n  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache\n}\n\n// Only one of these can be set:\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Deprecated (marked for migration)\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18; // New preferred field\n```\n\n**Migration Required**:\n- **If you set `disable_clear_route_cache: true`** → Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- **If you didn't set it (or set false)** → Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n**Before (v1.30)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Prevents route cache clearing\n```\n\n**After (v1.31)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Same behavior, new enum\n```\n\n**Key Behavioral Differences**:\n- `DEFAULT` (new): Allows external processor to control route cache via `clear_route_cache` field\n- `CLEAR`: Always clears route cache, overriding ext_proc response settings\n- `RETAIN`: Never clears route cache, equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### 2.2 Stream Pointer Management\n\n**Impact Level**: INTERNAL - Only affects custom filter implementations\n\nThe internal stream pointer management has changed in the Filter class:\n- **v1.30**: `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr)\n- **v1.31**: `ExternalProcessorStream* stream_` (raw pointer) + ThreadLocalStreamManager\n\nThis change enables deferred stream closure in observability mode. Standard users relying on the public API won't be affected.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Status**: Deprecated (not yet removed, but superseded)\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11) is deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum (field 18).\n\n**Timeline**:\n- **v1.31**: Both fields available, but `route_cache_action` is recommended\n- **v1.32+**: `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed\n\n**Migration Advice**:\nUpdate your configuration to use `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions:\n```yaml\n# Deprecated pattern (still works but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# Recommended pattern\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Important**: Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` should be set. The oneof field promotion in the proto ensures this constraint.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Enhanced Route Cache Control with `route_cache_action`\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nProvides three distinct strategies for handling route cache:\n\n#### Option 1: DEFAULT (Value: 0)\nAllows the external processor to control route cache clearing via the `clear_route_cache` field in `ProcessingResponse`.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You want the external processor to decide whether to clear the route cache based on header modifications or other factors.\n\n#### Option 2: CLEAR (Value: 1)\nAlways clears the route cache after external processor response, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Use Case**: External processing always modifies routing-relevant headers, so caching should be disabled.\n\n#### Option 3: RETAIN (Value: 2)\nNever clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the external processor.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You've verified that external processing never affects routing decisions, and want to avoid the performance cost of cache invalidation.\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure for Observability Mode\n\n**Field**: `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Default**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nIn observability mode, external processor streams are decoupled from the main HTTP request/response lifecycle. The `deferred_close_timeout` controls how long these streams remain open after the HTTP transaction completes.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 10  # Keep stream open for up to 10 seconds\n```\n\n**Internal Implementation**:\n- **New Classes**: `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager`\n- **Mechanism**: Streams are queued for deferred closure instead of being immediately deleted\n- **Cleanup**: A timeout timer ensures streams don't persist indefinitely\n\n**Behavioral Changes in Observability Mode**:\n\nIn v1.30, observability mode had limited deferred closure support. v1.31 adds:\n- Configurable deferred closure timeout\n- Proper stream lifecycle management\n- Thread-safe stream tracking via ThreadLocalStreamManager\n- Timeout-based cleanup to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: observability_processor\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 30  # Wait up to 30 seconds before closing stream\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### 4.3 Observability Mode Enhancements\n\n**Updated Features**:\n- Added `encodeComplete()` hook to ensure logging happens after entire response is sent\n- New `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` method for better header handling\n- New `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` method for body streaming without blocking\n- Enhanced `sendTrailers()` with observability mode awareness\n- New `buildHeaderRequest()` method supporting observability mode flag\n\n**Impact**:\nUsers enabling observability mode will benefit from:\n- Better separation of observability streams from request/response flow\n- Improved performance by not pausing filter chain execution\n- More robust timeout handling for external processor streams\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nIdentify all ext_proc filter configurations:\n\n```bash\n# Find all references to ext_proc in your Envoy configs\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/configs/\n```\n\nCheck if you use:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n- `observability_mode` field\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf your configuration uses route cache control:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Old way\n```\n\n**Migrate to v1.31**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # New way - equivalent behavior\n```\n\n**Decision Matrix**:\n\n| v1.30 Setting | v1.31 Equivalent | When to Use |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Processor controls cache clearing |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Processor never affects routing |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Processor always affects routing |\n\n### Step 3: Update Observability Mode Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf you use observability mode, explicitly configure the deferred close timeout:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration** (implicit default):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration** (explicit timeout):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout:\n      seconds: 5  # Explicitly set timeout (default is 5 seconds)\n```\n\n**Timeout Considerations**:\n- **Default (5 seconds)**: Good for most use cases, minimal memory overhead\n- **Longer timeout (10-30 seconds)**: For processors that need more time to flush data\n- **Shorter timeout (1-2 seconds)**: When memory is constrained, accept occasional stream interruptions\n\n### Step 4: Validate Proto Compatibility\n\nBefore deployment, verify your config validates against the new proto:\n\n```bash\n# Using envoy CLI (if available)\nenvoy -c config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or use protoc to validate\nprotoc --validate_out=/tmp ext_proc_config.textproto\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test in Staging Environment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy with updated configuration\n2. Verify ext_proc filter still processes requests correctly\n3. Check that route cache behavior matches expectations\n4. Monitor observability processor stream lifecycle (if using observability mode)\n\n**Key Tests**:\n- Route mutation behavior unchanged\n- Route cache clearing works as expected (use `CLEAR`, `DEFAULT`, or `RETAIN`)\n- Observability mode streams close properly and don't accumulate\n\n### Step 6: Deploy to Production\n\nOnce validated in staging:\n\n```bash\n# Gradual rollout recommended\ncanary_deployment(envoy_v1.31, percentage=10)\nmonitor_metrics()\nif errors_acceptable:\n  full_deployment(envoy_v1.31)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 6.1 Unit Testing\n\nCreate tests to verify route cache behavior:\n\n```python\n# Pseudocode for test cases\ntest_route_cache_action_default():\n  # Processor's clear_route_cache field should control cache clearing\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert route_cache_cleared()\n\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()\n\ntest_route_cache_action_clear():\n  # Cache should always be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert route_cache_cleared()  # Still cleared!\n\ntest_route_cache_action_retain():\n  # Cache should never be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()  # Still retained!\n\ntest_deferred_close_timeout():\n  # In observability mode, streams should close after timeout\n  enable_observability_mode()\n  set_deferred_close_timeout(seconds=1)\n\n  send_request()\n  assert_stream_open()\n\n  wait(milliseconds=1100)\n  assert_stream_closed()\n```\n\n### 6.2 Integration Testing\n\nTest with actual ext_proc processor:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 7.1 Quick Rollback (If Issues Occur)\n\nIf you experience problems after upgrading:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Revert Envoy to v1.30\ndeploy_envoy(version=1.30.0)\n\n# 2. Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### Pitfall 1: Setting Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting!\n```\n\n**Result**: One field takes precedence (undefined behavior depending on proto implementation)\n\n**Solution**: Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Clear choice\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Forgetting to Configure `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Problem**: Without explicit timeout configuration, default behavior applies but may not match your expectations.\n\n**Solution**: Be explicit:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Make it clear this is intentional\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Incorrect Route Cache Action Choice\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\n# Wrong: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Processor decides to clear (slower)\n```\n\n**Solution**: Match action to your processor's behavior:\n```yaml\n# Right: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear for correctness\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode Without Resource Limits\n\n**Problem**: Deferred streams in observability mode can accumulate if:\n- `deferred_close_timeout` is too long\n- External processor is slow to acknowledge\n- High request volume with many concurrent streams\n\n**Solution**: Monitor and tune:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Keep it reasonable (default is good)\n  # Consider separate resource limits for observability streams\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Compatibility Matrix\n\n| Feature | v1.30 | v1.31 | Backward Compat |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Basic ext_proc functionality | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | ✓ | ✓* | Deprecated |\n| `route_cache_action` | ✗ | ✓ | N/A |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | ✗ | ✓ | N/A |\n| Observability mode | ✓ | ✓† | Enhanced |\n| Processing modes | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n| Metadata options | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n| Header mutation rules | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n\n**Legend**:\n- ✓ = Supported\n- ✗ = Not supported\n- ✓* = Supported but deprecated\n- ✓† = Supported with enhancements\n\n---\n\n## 10. Reference: Proto Changes Detail\n\n### Imports Added\n```protobuf\n// Added in v1.31\nimport \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n```\n\n### New Enum\n```protobuf\n// New in v1.31 (field 102-120)\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Protobuf comment: The default behavior is to clear the route cache\n  // only when the clear_route_cache field is set in the external\n  // processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is\n  // equivalent to setting disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n### Field Changes\n```protobuf\n// v1.30\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n// v1.31 - with deprecation migration annotation\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n// v1.31 - new field\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n// v1.31 - new field\ngoogle.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 12. Frequently Asked Questions\n\n### Q: Do I have to update my configuration immediately?\n\n**A**: No. Both configurations work in v1.31, but we recommend updating to `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions where `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed.\n\n### Q: What happens if I don't set `route_cache_action`?\n\n**A**: It defaults to `DEFAULT`, which means the external processor can control route cache clearing. This matches the behavior of `disable_clear_route_cache: false` in v1.30.\n\n### Q: Does deferred_close_timeout affect request latency?\n\n**A**: No. The timeout only applies to the external processor stream in observability mode, after the HTTP response is complete. It doesn't affect request/response processing.\n\n### Q: Can I still use `disable_clear_route_cache` in v1.31?\n\n**A**: Yes, but it's deprecated. Prefer `route_cache_action` for clarity and future compatibility.\n\n### Q: What's the performance impact of v1.31?\n\n**A**: Negligible for non-observability-mode deployments. Observability mode may use slightly more memory due to deferred stream management, but this is temporary and controlled by timeout.\n\n### Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?\n\n**A**:\n- Use `DEFAULT` if your external processor sometimes modifies routing headers\n- Use `CLEAR` if your external processor always modifies routing headers\n- Use `RETAIN` if your external processor never modifies routing headers\n\n---\n\n## 13. Overview\n     7→\n     8→The Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:\n     9→\n    10→- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag\n    11→- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow\n    12→- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode\n    13→- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout\n    14→\n    15→This migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.\n    16→\n    17→---\n    18→\n    19→## 2. Breaking Changes\n    20→\n    21→### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior\n    22→\n    23→**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required\n    24→\n    25→In v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:\n    26→```protobuf\n    27→// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto\n    28→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n    29→```\n    30→\n    31→In v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:\n    32→```protobuf\n    33→// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto\n    34→enum RouteCacheAction {\n    35→  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache\n    36→  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache\n    37→  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache\n    38→}\n    39→\n    40→// Only one of these can be set:\n    41→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Deprecated (marked for migration)\n    42→RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18; // New preferred field\n    43→```\n    44→\n    45→**Migration Required**:\n    46→- **If you set `disable_clear_route_cache: true`** → Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n    47→- **If you didn't set it (or set false)** → Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n    48→\n    49→**Before (v1.30)**:\n    50→```yaml\n    51→ext_proc:\n    52→  grpc_service:\n    53→    envoy_grpc:\n    54→      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    55→  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Prevents route cache clearing\n    56→```\n    57→\n    58→**After (v1.31)**:\n    59→```yaml\n    60→ext_proc:\n    61→  grpc_service:\n    62→    envoy_grpc:\n    63→      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n    64→  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Same behavior, new enum\n    65→```\n    66→\n    67→**Key Behavioral Differences**:\n    68→- `DEFAULT` (new): Allows external processor to control route cache via `clear_route_cache` field\n    69→- `CLEAR`: Always clears route cache, overriding ext_proc response settings\n    70→- `RETAIN`: Never clears route cache, equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n    71→\n    72→### 2.2 Stream Pointer Management\n    73→\n    74→**Impact Level**: INTERNAL - Only affects custom filter implementations\n    75→\n    76→The internal stream pointer management has changed in the Filter class:\n    77→- **v1.30**: `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr)\n    78→- **v1.31**: `ExternalProcessorStream* stream_` (raw pointer) + ThreadLocalStreamManager\n    79→\n    80→This change enables deferred stream closure in observability mode. Standard users relying on the public API won't be affected.\n    81→\n    82→---\n    83→\n    84→## 3. Deprecated Features\n    85→\n    86→### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n    87→\n    88→**Status**: Deprecated (not yet removed, but superseded)\n    89→\n    90→The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11) is deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum (field 18).\n    91→\n    92→**Timeline**:\n    93→- **v1.31**: Both fields available, but `route_cache_action` is recommended\n    94→- **v1.32+**: `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed\n    95→\n    96→**Migration Advice**:\n    97→Update your configuration to use `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions:\n    98→```yaml\n    99→# Deprecated pattern (still works but not recommended)\n   100→disable_clear_route_cache: true\n   101→\n   102→# Recommended pattern\n   103→route_cache_action: RETAIN\n   104→```\n   105→\n   106→**Important**: Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` should be set. The oneof field promotion in the proto ensures this constraint.\n   107→\n   108→---\n   109→\n   110→## 4. New Features\n   111→\n   112→### 4.1 Enhanced Route Cache Control with `route_cache_action`\n   113→\n   114→**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n   115→**Type**: `RouteCacheAction` enum\n   116→**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n   117→\n   118→Provides three distinct strategies for handling route cache:\n   119→\n   120→#### Option 1: DEFAULT (Value: 0)\n   121→Allows the external processor to control route cache clearing via the `clear_route_cache` field in `ProcessingResponse`.\n   122→\n   123→```yaml\n   124→ext_proc:\n   125→  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n   126→```\n   127→\n   128→**Use Case**: You want the external processor to decide whether to clear the route cache based on header modifications or other factors.\n   129→\n   130→#### Option 2: CLEAR (Value: 1)\n   131→Always clears the route cache after external processor response, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field.\n   132→\n   133→```yaml\n   134→ext_proc:\n   135→  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n   136→```\n   137→\n   138→**Use Case**: External processing always modifies routing-relevant headers, so caching should be disabled.\n   139→\n   140→#### Option 3: RETAIN (Value: 2)\n   141→Never clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the external processor.\n   142→\n   143→```yaml\n   144→ext_proc:\n   145→  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n   146→```\n   147→\n   148→**Use Case**: You've verified that external processing never affects routing decisions, and want to avoid the performance cost of cache invalidation.\n   149→\n   150→### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure for Observability Mode\n   151→\n   152→**Field**: `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n   153→**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n   154→**Default**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n   155→**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n   156→\n   157→In observability mode, external processor streams are decoupled from the main HTTP request/response lifecycle. The `deferred_close_timeout` controls how long these streams remain open after the HTTP transaction completes.\n   158→\n   159→```yaml\n   160→ext_proc:\n   161→  observability_mode: true\n   162→  deferred_close_timeout:\n   163→    seconds: 10  # Keep stream open for up to 10 seconds\n   164→```\n   165→\n   166→**Internal Implementation**:\n   167→- **New Classes**: `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager`\n   168→- **Mechanism**: Streams are queued for deferred closure instead of being immediately deleted\n   169→- **Cleanup**: A timeout timer ensures streams don't persist indefinitely\n   170→\n   171→**Behavioral Changes in Observability Mode**:\n   172→\n   173→In v1.30, observability mode had limited deferred closure support. v1.31 adds:\n   174→- Configurable deferred closure timeout\n   175→- Proper stream lifecycle management\n   176→- Thread-safe stream tracking via ThreadLocalStreamManager\n   177→- Timeout-based cleanup to prevent resource exhaustion\n   178→\n   179→**Configuration Example**:\n   180→```yaml\n   181→ext_proc:\n   182→  grpc_service:\n   183→    envoy_grpc:\n   184→      cluster_name: observability_processor\n   185→  observability_mode: true\n   186→  deferred_close_timeout:\n   187→    seconds: 30  # Wait up to 30 seconds before closing stream\n   188→  processing_mode:\n   189→    request_header_mode: SEND\n   190→    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n   191→    response_header_mode: SEND\n   192→    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n   193→```\n   194→\n   195→### 4.3 Observability Mode Enhancements\n   196→\n   197→**Updated Features**:\n   198→- Added `encodeComplete()` hook to ensure logging happens after entire response is sent\n   199→- New `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` method for better header handling\n   200→- New `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` method for body streaming without blocking\n   201→- Enhanced `sendTrailers()` with observability mode awareness\n   202→- New `buildHeaderRequest()` method supporting observability mode flag\n   203→\n   204→**Impact**:\n   205→Users enabling observability mode will benefit from:\n   206→- Better separation of observability streams from request/response flow\n   207→- Improved performance by not pausing filter chain execution\n   208→- More robust timeout handling for external processor streams\n   209→\n   210→---\n   211→\n   212→## 5. Migration Steps\n   213→\n   214→### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n   215→\n   216→Identify all ext_proc filter configurations:\n   217→\n   218→```bash\n   219→# Find all references to ext_proc in your Envoy configs\n   220→grep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/configs/\n   221→```\n   222→\n   223→Check if you use:\n   224→- `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n   225→- `observability_mode` field\n   226→\n   227→### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration (If Used)\n   228→\n   229→If your configuration uses route cache control:\n   230→\n   231→**v1.30 Configuration**:\n   232→```yaml\n   233→http_filters:\n   234→- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n   235→  typed_config:\n   236→    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n   237→    grpc_service:\n   238→      envoy_grpc:\n   239→        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n   240→    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Old way\n   241→```\n   242→\n   243→**Migrate to v1.31**:\n   244→```yaml\n   245→http_filters:\n   246→- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n   247→  typed_config:\n   248→    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n   249→    grpc_service:\n   250→      envoy_grpc:\n   251→        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n   252→    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # New way - equivalent behavior\n   253→```\n   254→\n   255→**Decision Matrix**:\n   256→\n   257→| v1.30 Setting | v1.31 Equivalent | When to Use |\n   258→|---|---|---|\n   259→| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Processor controls cache clearing |\n   260→| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Processor never affects routing |\n   261→| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Processor always affects routing |\n   262→\n   263→### Step 3: Update Observability Mode Configuration (If Used)\n   264→\n   265→If you use observability mode, explicitly configure the deferred close timeout:\n   266→\n   267→**v1.30 Configuration** (implicit default):\n   268→```yaml\n   269→http_filters:\n   270→- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n   271→  typed_config:\n   272→    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n   273→    grpc_service:\n   274→      envoy_grpc:\n   275→        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n   276→    observability_mode: true\n   277→```\n   278→\n   279→**v1.31 Configuration** (explicit timeout):\n   280→```yaml\n   281→http_filters:\n   282→- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n   283→  typed_config:\n   284→    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n   285→    grpc_service:\n   286→      envoy_grpc:\n   287→        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n   288→    observability_mode: true\n   289→    deferred_close_timeout:\n   290→      seconds: 5  # Explicitly set timeout (default is 5 seconds)\n   291→```\n   292→\n   293→**Timeout Considerations**:\n   294→- **Default (5 seconds)**: Good for most use cases, minimal memory overhead\n   295→- **Longer timeout (10-30 seconds)**: For processors that need more time to flush data\n   296→- **Shorter timeout (1-2 seconds)**: When memory is constrained, accept occasional stream interruptions\n   297→\n   298→### Step 4: Validate Proto Compatibility\n   299→\n   300→Before deployment, verify your config validates against the new proto:\n   301→\n   302→```bash\n   303→# Using envoy CLI (if available)\n   304→envoy -c config.yaml --mode validate\n   305→\n   306→# Or use protoc to validate\n   307→protoc --validate_out=/tmp ext_proc_config.textproto\n   308→```\n   309→\n   310→### Step 5: Test in Staging Environment\n   311→\n   312→1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy with updated configuration\n   313→2. Verify ext_proc filter still processes requests correctly\n   314→3. Check that route cache behavior matches expectations\n   315→4. Monitor observability processor stream lifecycle (if using observability mode)\n   316→\n   317→**Key Tests**:\n   318→- Route mutation behavior unchanged\n   319→- Route cache clearing works as expected (use `CLEAR`, `DEFAULT`, or `RETAIN`)\n   320→- Observability mode streams close properly and don't accumulate\n   321→\n   322→### Step 6: Deploy to Production\n   323→\n   324→Once validated in staging:\n   325→\n   326→```bash\n   327→# Gradual rollout recommended\n   328→canary_deployment(envoy_v1.31, percentage=10)\n   329→monitor_metrics()\n   330→if errors_acceptable:\n   331→  full_deployment(envoy_v1.31)\n   332→```\n   333→\n   334→---\n   335→\n   336→## 6. Testing Recommendations\n   337→\n   338→### 6.1 Unit Testing\n   339→\n   340→Create tests to verify route cache behavior:\n   341→\n   342→```python\n   343→# Pseudocode for test cases\n   344→test_route_cache_action_default():\n   345→  # Processor's clear_route_cache field should control cache clearing\n   346→  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n   347→  assert route_cache_cleared()\n   348→\n   349→  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n   350→  assert not route_cache_cleared()\n   351→\n   352→test_route_cache_action_clear():\n   353→  # Cache should always be cleared regardless of processor response\n   354→  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n   355→  assert route_cache_cleared()  # Still cleared!\n   356→\n   357→test_route_cache_action_retain():\n   358→  # Cache should never be cleared regardless of processor response\n   359→  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n   360→  assert not route_cache_cleared()  # Still retained!\n   361→\n   362→test_deferred_close_timeout():\n   363→  # In observability mode, streams should close after timeout\n   364→  enable_observability_mode()\n   365→  set_deferred_close_timeout(seconds=1)\n   366→\n   367→  send_request()\n   368→  assert_stream_open()\n   369→\n   370→  wait(milliseconds=1100)\n   371→  assert_stream_closed()\n   372→```\n   373→\n   374→### 6.2 Integration Testing\n   375→\n   376→Test with actual ext_proc processor:\n   377→\n   378→```bash\n   379→# 1. Deploy test ext_proc service\n   380→docker run -d test_ext_proc_service\n   381→\n   382→# 2. Test route cache clearing behavior\n   383→curl http://envoy:10000/api/test-route-cache \\\n   384→  -H \"X-Modify-Route-Header: true\"\n   385→\n   386→# Verify: Route cache behavior matches configuration\n   387→\n   388→# 3. Test observability mode (if enabled)\n   389→curl http://envoy:10000/api/test-observability\n   390→\n   391→# Verify:\n   392→# - Request completes immediately\n   393→# - Processor stream stays open for configured timeout\n   394→# - No stream accumulation over time\n   395→```\n   396→\n   397→### 6.3 Performance Testing\n   398→\n   399→Compare v1.30 vs v1.31 under load:\n   400→\n   401→**Metrics to Monitor**:\n   402→- Request latency (should be identical)\n   403→- Memory usage (especially in observability mode)\n   404→- gRPC stream count (should stabilize around expected number)\n   405→- Route cache hit rate (shouldn't change)\n   406→\n   407→**Load Test Scenario**:\n   408→```\n   409→- Concurrent requests: 1000\n   410→- Request rate: 10,000 req/s\n   411→- Duration: 5 minutes\n   412→- Observability mode: enabled with 5s timeout\n   413→```\n   414→\n   415→Expected Results:\n   416→- Latency: ±5% of v1.30\n   417→- Memory: Similar to v1.30 (deferred streams are temporary)\n   418→- Streams: Should match concurrent request count + observability overhead\n   419→\n   420→---\n   421→\n   422→## 7. Rollback Guidance\n   423→\n   424→### 7.1 Quick Rollback (If Issues Occur)\n   425→\n   426→If you experience problems after upgrading:\n   427→\n   428→```bash\n   429→# 1. Revert Envoy to v1.30\n   430→deploy_envoy(version=1.30.0)\n   431→\n   432→# 2. Revert configuration\n   433→revert_config(git_commit=last_working)\n   434→\n   435→# 3. Common Migration Pitfalls\n   473→\n   474→### Pitfall 1: Setting Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n   475→\n   476→**Problem**:\n   477→```yaml\n   478→ext_proc:\n   479→  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n   480→  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting!\n   481→```\n   482→\n   483→**Result**: One field takes precedence (undefined behavior depending on proto implementation)\n   484→\n   485→**Solution**: Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31:\n   486→```yaml\n   487→ext_proc:\n   488→  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Clear choice\n   489→```\n   490→\n   491→### Pitfall 2: Forgetting to Configure `deferred_close_timeout`\n   492→\n   493→**Problem**: Without explicit timeout configuration, default behavior applies but may not match your expectations.\n   494→\n   495→**Solution**: Be explicit:\n   496→```yaml\n   497→ext_proc:\n   498→  observability_mode: true\n   499→  deferred_close_timeout:\n   500→    seconds: 5  # Make it clear this is intentional\n   501→```\n   502→\n   503→### Pitfall 3: Incorrect Route Cache Action Choice\n   504→\n   505→**Problem**:\n   506→```yaml\n   507→# Wrong: Processor always modifies routing headers\n   508→ext_proc:\n   509→  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Processor decides to clear (slower)\n   510→```\n   511→\n   512→**Solution**: Match action to your processor's behavior:\n   513→```yaml\n   514→# Right: Processor always modifies routing headers\n   515→ext_proc:\n   516→  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear for correctness\n   517→```\n   518→\n   519→### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode Without Resource Limits\n   520→\n   521→**Problem**: Deferred streams in observability mode can accumulate if:\n   522→- `deferred_close_timeout` is too long\n   523→- External processor is slow to acknowledge\n   524→- High request volume with many concurrent streams\n   525→\n   526→**Solution**: Monitor and tune:\n   527→```yaml\n   528→ext_proc:\n   529→  observability_mode: true\n   530→  deferred_close_timeout:\n   531→    seconds: 5  # Keep it reasonable (default is good)\n   532→  # Consider separate resource limits for observability streams\n   533→```\n   534→\n   535→---\n   536→\n   537→## 9. Compatibility Matrix\n   538→\n   539→| Feature | v1.30 | v1.31 | Backward Compat |\n   540→|---|---|---|---|\n   541→| Basic ext_proc functionality | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n   542→| `disable_clear_route_cache` | ✓ | ✓* | Deprecated |\n   543→| `route_cache_action` | ✗ | ✓ | N/A |\n   544→| `deferred_close_timeout` | ✗ | ✓ | N/A |\n   545→| Observability mode | ✓ | ✓† | Enhanced |\n   546→| Processing modes | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n   547→| Metadata options | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n   548→| Header mutation rules | ✓ | ✓ | Full |\n   549→\n   550→**Legend**:\n   551→- ✓ = Supported\n   552→- ✗ = Not supported\n   553→- ✓* = Supported but deprecated\n   554→- ✓† = Supported with enhancements\n   555→\n   556→---\n   557→\n   558→## 10. Reference: Proto Changes Detail\n   668→\n   669→### Imports Added\n   670→```protobuf\n   671→// Added in v1.31\n   672→import \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n   673→```\n   674→\n   675→### New Enum\n   676→```protobuf\n   677→// New in v1.31 (field 102-120)\n   678→enum RouteCacheAction {\n   679→  // Protobuf comment: The default behavior is to clear the route cache\n   680→  // only when the clear_route_cache field is set in the external\n   681→  // processor response.\n   682→  DEFAULT = 0;\n   683→\n   684→  // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n   685→  // bit in the external processor response.\n   686→  CLEAR = 1;\n   687→\n   688→  // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache\n   689→  // bit in the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is\n   690→  // equivalent to setting disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n   691→  RETAIN = 2;\n   692→}\n   693→```\n   694→\n   695→### Field Changes\n   696→```protobuf\n   697→// v1.30\n   698→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n   699→\n   700→// v1.31 - with deprecation migration annotation\n   701→bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n   702→    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n   703→\n   704→// v1.31 - new field\n   705→RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n   706→    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n   707→\n   708→// v1.31 - new field\n   709→google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n   710→```\n   711→\n   712→---\n   713→\n   714→## 12. Frequently Asked Questions\n   715→\n   716→### Q: Do I have to update my configuration immediately?\n   717→\n   718→**A**: No. Both configurations work in v1.31, but we recommend updating to `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions where `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed.\n   719→\n   720→### Q: What happens if I don't set `route_cache_action`?\n   721→\n   722→**A**: It defaults to `DEFAULT`, which means the external processor can control route cache clearing. This matches the behavior of `disable_clear_route_cache: false` in v1.30.\n   723→\n   724→### Q: Does deferred_close_timeout affect request latency?\n   725→\n   726→**A**: No. The timeout only applies to the external processor stream in observability mode, after the HTTP response is complete. It doesn't affect request/response processing.\n   727→\n   728→### Q: Can I still use `disable_clear_route_cache` in v1.31?\n   729→\n   730→**A**: Yes, but it's deprecated. Prefer `route_cache_action` for clarity and future compatibility.\n   731→\n   732→### Q: What's the performance impact of v1.31?\n   733→\n   734→**A**: Negligible for non-observability-mode deployments. Observability mode may use slightly more memory due to deferred stream management, but this is temporary and controlled by timeout.\n   735→\n   736→### Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?\n   737→\n   738→**A**:\n   739→- Use `DEFAULT` if your external processor sometimes modifies routing headers\n   740→- Use `CLEAR` if your external processor always modifies routing headers\n   741→- Use `RETAIN` if your external processor never modifies routing headers\n   742→\n   743→---\n   744→\n   745→## 13. Overview\n\nThe Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter migration from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0 introduces several important improvements focused on:\n\n- **Route Cache Control**: Enhanced route cache handling with an enum-based approach replacing the boolean flag\n- **Observability Mode Enhancements**: Improved support for observing HTTP traffic without affecting request/response flow\n- **Stream Lifecycle Management**: Better control over gRPC stream closure, especially in observability mode\n- **Deferred Stream Closure**: New mechanism to properly defer external processor stream closure with configurable timeout\n\nThis migration is relatively non-disruptive, but involves configuration changes and behavioral updates for users relying on route cache controls and observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Control Behavior\n\n**Impact Level**: HIGH - Configuration change required\n\nIn v1.30, route cache control was a simple boolean:\n```protobuf\n// v1.30 - ext_proc.proto\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31, this has been replaced with an enum-based approach:\n```protobuf\n// v1.31 - ext_proc.proto\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;   // Default: clear cache when ext_proc response sets clear_route_cache\n  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear route cache\n  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear route cache\n}\n\n// Only one of these can be set:\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;      // Deprecated (marked for migration)\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18; // New preferred field\n```\n\n**Migration Required**:\n- **If you set `disable_clear_route_cache: true`** → Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- **If you didn't set it (or set false)** → Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n**Before (v1.30)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Prevents route cache clearing\n```\n\n**After (v1.31)**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Same behavior, new enum\n```\n\n**Key Behavioral Differences**:\n- `DEFAULT` (new): Allows external processor to control route cache via `clear_route_cache` field\n- `CLEAR`: Always clears route cache, overriding ext_proc response settings\n- `RETAIN`: Never clears route cache, equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n### 2.2 Stream Pointer Management\n\n**Impact Level**: INTERNAL - Only affects custom filter implementations\n\nThe internal stream pointer management has changed in the Filter class:\n- **v1.30**: `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr)\n- **v1.31**: `ExternalProcessorStream* stream_` (raw pointer) + ThreadLocalStreamManager\n\nThis change enables deferred stream closure in observability mode. Standard users relying on the public API won't be affected.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Status**: Deprecated (not yet removed, but superseded)\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field (field 11) is deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum (field 18).\n\n**Timeline**:\n- **v1.31**: Both fields available, but `route_cache_action` is recommended\n- **v1.32+**: `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed\n\n**Migration Advice**:\nUpdate your configuration to use `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions:\n```yaml\n# Deprecated pattern (still works but not recommended)\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# Recommended pattern\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Important**: Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` should be set. The oneof field promotion in the proto ensures this constraint.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Enhanced Route Cache Control with `route_cache_action`\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nProvides three distinct strategies for handling route cache:\n\n#### Option 1: DEFAULT (Value: 0)\nAllows the external processor to control route cache clearing via the `clear_route_cache` field in `ProcessingResponse`.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You want the external processor to decide whether to clear the route cache based on header modifications or other factors.\n\n#### Option 2: CLEAR (Value: 1)\nAlways clears the route cache after external processor response, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Use Case**: External processing always modifies routing-relevant headers, so caching should be disabled.\n\n#### Option 3: RETAIN (Value: 2)\nNever clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the external processor.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Use Case**: You've verified that external processing never affects routing decisions, and want to avoid the performance cost of cache invalidation.\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure for Observability Mode\n\n**Field**: `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19)\n**Type**: `google.protobuf.Duration`\n**Default**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n**Scope**: ExternalProcessor message\n\nIn observability mode, external processor streams are decoupled from the main HTTP request/response lifecycle. The `deferred_close_timeout` controls how long these streams remain open after the HTTP transaction completes.\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 10  # Keep stream open for up to 10 seconds\n```\n\n**Internal Implementation**:\n- **New Classes**: `DeferredDeletableStream` and `ThreadLocalStreamManager`\n- **Mechanism**: Streams are queued for deferred closure instead of being immediately deleted\n- **Cleanup**: A timeout timer ensures streams don't persist indefinitely\n\n**Behavioral Changes in Observability Mode**:\n\nIn v1.30, observability mode had limited deferred closure support. v1.31 adds:\n- Configurable deferred closure timeout\n- Proper stream lifecycle management\n- Thread-safe stream tracking via ThreadLocalStreamManager\n- Timeout-based cleanup to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: observability_processor\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 30  # Wait up to 30 seconds before closing stream\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### 4.3 Observability Mode Enhancements\n\n**Updated Features**:\n- Added `encodeComplete()` hook to ensure logging happens after entire response is sent\n- New `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` method for better header handling\n- New `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` method for body streaming without blocking\n- Enhanced `sendTrailers()` with observability mode awareness\n- New `buildHeaderRequest()` method supporting observability mode flag\n\n**Impact**:\nUsers enabling observability mode will benefit from:\n- Better separation of observability streams from request/response flow\n- Improved performance by not pausing filter chain execution\n- More robust timeout handling for external processor streams\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Assess Current Configuration\n\nIdentify all ext_proc filter configurations:\n\n```bash\n# Find all references to ext_proc in your Envoy configs\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/configs/\n```\n\nCheck if you use:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache` field\n- `observability_mode` field\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf your configuration uses route cache control:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Old way\n```\n\n**Migrate to v1.31**:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # New way - equivalent behavior\n```\n\n**Decision Matrix**:\n\n| v1.30 Setting | v1.31 Equivalent | When to Use |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Processor controls cache clearing |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Processor never affects routing |\n| N/A | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | Processor always affects routing |\n\n### Step 3: Update Observability Mode Configuration (If Used)\n\nIf you use observability mode, explicitly configure the deferred close timeout:\n\n**v1.30 Configuration** (implicit default):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration** (explicit timeout):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout:\n      seconds: 5  # Explicitly set timeout (default is 5 seconds)\n```\n\n**Timeout Considerations**:\n- **Default (5 seconds)**: Good for most use cases, minimal memory overhead\n- **Longer timeout (10-30 seconds)**: For processors that need more time to flush data\n- **Shorter timeout (1-2 seconds)**: When memory is constrained, accept occasional stream interruptions\n\n### Step 4: Validate Proto Compatibility\n\nBefore deployment, verify your config validates against the new proto:\n\n```bash\n# Using envoy CLI (if available)\nenvoy -c config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or use protoc to validate\nprotoc --validate_out=/tmp ext_proc_config.textproto\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test in Staging Environment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31 Envoy with updated configuration\n2. Verify ext_proc filter still processes requests correctly\n3. Check that route cache behavior matches expectations\n4. Monitor observability processor stream lifecycle (if using observability mode)\n\n**Key Tests**:\n- Route mutation behavior unchanged\n- Route cache clearing works as expected (use `CLEAR`, `DEFAULT`, or `RETAIN`)\n- Observability mode streams close properly and don't accumulate\n\n### Step 6: Deploy to Production\n\nOnce validated in staging:\n\n```bash\n# Gradual rollout recommended\ncanary_deployment(envoy_v1.31, percentage=10)\nmonitor_metrics()\nif errors_acceptable:\n  full_deployment(envoy_v1.31)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 6.1 Unit Testing\n\nCreate tests to verify route cache behavior:\n\n```python\n# Pseudocode for test cases\ntest_route_cache_action_default():\n  # Processor's clear_route_cache field should control cache clearing\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert route_cache_cleared()\n\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()\n\ntest_route_cache_action_clear():\n  # Cache should always be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = False\n  assert route_cache_cleared()  # Still cleared!\n\ntest_route_cache_action_retain():\n  # Cache should never be cleared regardless of processor response\n  ext_proc_response.clear_route_cache = True\n  assert not route_cache_cleared()  # Still retained!\n\ntest_deferred_close_timeout():\n  # In observability mode, streams should close after timeout\n  enable_observability_mode()\n  set_deferred_close_timeout(seconds=1)\n\n  send_request()\n  assert_stream_open()\n\n  wait(milliseconds=1100)\n  assert_stream_closed()\n```\n\n### 6.2 Integration Testing\n\nTest with actual ext_proc processor:\n\n```bash\n# 1. Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### Pitfall 1: Setting Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Conflicting!\n```\n\n**Result**: One field takes precedence (undefined behavior depending on proto implementation)\n\n**Solution**: Use only `route_cache_action` in v1.31:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Clear choice\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Forgetting to Configure `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Problem**: Without explicit timeout configuration, default behavior applies but may not match your expectations.\n\n**Solution**: Be explicit:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Make it clear this is intentional\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Incorrect Route Cache Action Choice\n\n**Problem**:\n```yaml\n# Wrong: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Processor decides to clear (slower)\n```\n\n**Solution**: Match action to your processor's behavior:\n```yaml\n# Right: Processor always modifies routing headers\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear for correctness\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Observability Mode Without Resource Limits\n\n**Problem**: Deferred streams in observability mode can accumulate if:\n- `deferred_close_timeout` is too long\n- External processor is slow to acknowledge\n- High request volume with many concurrent streams\n\n**Solution**: Monitor and tune:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 5  # Keep it reasonable (default is good)\n  # Consider separate resource limits for observability streams\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Frequently Asked Questions\n\n### Q: Do I have to update my configuration immediately?\n\n**A**: No. Both configurations work in v1.31, but we recommend updating to `route_cache_action` to prepare for future versions where `disable_clear_route_cache` may be removed.\n\n### Q: What happens if I don't set `route_cache_action`?\n\n**A**: It defaults to `DEFAULT`, which means the external processor can control route cache clearing. This matches the behavior of `disable_clear_route_cache: false` in v1.30.\n\n### Q: Does deferred_close_timeout affect request latency?\n\n**A**: No. The timeout only applies to the external processor stream in observability mode, after the HTTP response is complete. It doesn't affect request/response processing.\n\n### Q: Can I still use `disable_clear_route_cache` in v1.31?\n\n**A**: Yes, but it's deprecated. Prefer `route_cache_action` for clarity and future compatibility.\n\n### Q: What's the performance impact of v1.31?\n\n**A**: Negligible for non-observability-mode deployments. Observability mode may use slightly more memory due to deferred stream management, but this is temporary and controlled by timeout.\n\n### Q: How do I know which `route_cache_action` to use?\n\n**A**:\n- Use `DEFAULT` if your external processor sometimes modifies routing headers\n- Use `CLEAR` if your external processor always modifies routing headers\n- Use `RETAIN` if your external processor never modifies routing headers\n\n---\n\n## 13.
